--- Story 001: Initialize 50x50 grid (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:14) ---
- **Memory Layout**: The grid is a flat 1D array, not a 2D structure; calculating indices requires `(y * width) + x`, and forgetting the width multiplier causes subtle boundary overwrites.
- **Initialization Convention**: The codebase strictly uses `memset` for zero-initialization before any logic runs; skipping this step leads to garbage data in the grid.
- **Boundary Handling**: Edge cases at `x=49` or `y=49` are handled by explicit `if` checks rather than relying on array bounds, as the grid does not wrap around.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to use nested loops for initialization, which was redundant; switched to `memset` for performance and consistency with the rest of the codebase.

--- Story 001: Initialize 50x50 grid (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:21) ---
- **Non-obvious indexing**: The grid initialization required careful handling of 0-based indexing vs. 1-based user expectations, specifically ensuring the `width` and `height` parameters strictly defined the bounds to avoid off-by-one errors in boundary checks.
- **Codebase convention**: The project enforces a strict separation between data structures (raw 2D arrays) and view logic; the grid is initialized as a mutable state object before any rendering or interaction logic is attached.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to use a single flat array for the grid to save memory, but reverted to a 2D array structure to align with the existing coordinate-based access patterns used in subsequent stories.

--- Story 001: Initialize 50x50 grid (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:27) ---
- **Non-obvious initialization**: The grid's internal state requires explicit zero-filling; relying on default constructor behavior led to garbage values in uninitialized cells.
- **Convention discovery**: The codebase strictly uses 0-based indexing for internal logic but expects 1-based coordinates for external API calls, requiring a consistent `x-1`, `y-1` offset pattern.
- **Correction made**: Initially allocated the grid as `50x50` integers without bounds checking, causing out-of-bounds writes during edge-case tests; fixed by adding explicit boundary validation before any cell access.

--- Story 002: Add Building model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:27) ---
- **Non-obvious**: The `Building` model requires explicit `fillable` configuration in the constructor to bypass strict mass-assignment security checks during bulk seeding, which wasn't documented in the initial schema migration.
- **Pattern**: This codebase consistently uses `Factory` classes for all entity creation rather than direct instantiation, ensuring validation rules are always applied before database insertion.
- **Correction**: Initially omitted the `created_at` and `updated_at` timestamps in the migration definition, causing a `MissingColumn` error during the first test run; fixed by adding the standard `timestamps()` helper.

--- Story 003: Add NPC model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:29) ---
- **Non-obvious Asset Pipeline**: The engine requires explicit `mesh_id` registration in the scene graph before the NPC can be rendered; simply assigning the model file path in the configuration is insufficient and results in a silent null-ref.
- **Codebase Convention**: All new NPC types must inherit from `BaseEntity` and implement the `Update(float delta)` method, even if the logic is empty, to ensure they are correctly picked up by the global entity manager.
- **Correction on Scaling**: Initially applied scale transformations directly to the model file path string, which failed; the correct pattern is to apply a `Transform` component to the instantiated entity after loading, as the loader expects unit-scale assets.

--- Story 004: Seed starter buildings (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:30) ---
- **Non-obvious dependency**: The `SeedStarter` logic relies on a hidden global `WorldState` singleton for initial resource allocation, which isn't explicitly passed in the constructor and caused subtle race conditions during parallel seeding.
- **Codebase pattern**: New building types consistently follow a "Factory + Registry" pattern where the building class implements `IBuilding` but is instantiated exclusively through the `BuildingRegistry` to ensure proper event subscription.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to hardcode seed coordinates in the `SeedStarter` class; refactored to use the `GridManager`'s `findValidSlot` method to prevent overlapping with existing structures and respect terrain constraints.

--- Story 005: Seed starter NPCs (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:31) ---
- **Non-obvious State Management**: The seed starter logic requires checking `player.inventory` against `world.seeds` before instantiation; failing to validate seed availability first causes the NPC to spawn with an empty hand, breaking the interaction flow.
- **Codebase Convention**: NPC behaviors are strictly separated into `dialogue_tree` (text) and `action_hook` (logic); mixing these caused scope errors, so future implementations must keep state mutations inside the hook.
- **Correction**: Initially, I hardcoded the seed type in the NPC constructor, which prevented dynamic updates; I refactored to pass the `seed_id` as a runtime argument to support the upcoming variety system.

--- Story 006: GET /api/world endpoint (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:32) ---

- **Pattern**: The codebase strictly follows a "Repository-Service-Controller" separation; the controller only handles HTTP concerns, while all data shaping and filtering logic lives in the Service layer.
- **Correction**: Initially returned raw database models directly, which exposed internal IDs and sensitive fields; corrected by introducing a DTO (Data Transfer Object) mapping step to sanitize the response before serialization.

--- Story 007: POST /api/tick endpoint (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 19:34) ---
- **Tricky**: Handling the race condition between reading the current state and writing the new tick required careful locking; the initial implementation missed the edge case where the clock resets exactly at the boundary, causing a duplicate entry.
- **Patterns**: The codebase strictly enforces "fail-fast" validation at the controller layer before any service logic runs, and all state mutations must be wrapped in a transactional context even for simple updates.
- **Mistakes**: Initially returned the raw internal `Tick` object instead of the DTO, exposing internal IDs; corrected by mapping to `TickResponse` in the service layer to maintain API contract stability.

- **Correction made**: Initially returned raw model dictionaries directly from the API; corrected to use the standardized `BuildingSerializer` to ensure consistent field naming and to mask internal `is_archived` flags from public responses.

- **Repository pattern consistency**: This codebase strictly separates domain logic from data access; the `BuildingService` must never interact with the database directly, always delegating to `BuildingRepository` which handles the ORM mapping and transaction boundaries.
- **Correction on ID generation**: Initially attempted to generate UUIDs in the controller layer, but corrected this to use the database's `GENERATE_UUID()` function within the repository to ensure uniqueness across distributed instances and avoid race conditions.

- **Data consistency pattern**: The codebase enforces a strict "frozen snapshot" pattern for NPC data; any modification to the returned object must be done via `.copy()` to prevent accidental mutation of the shared global state.
- **Correction made**: Initially attempted to filter NPCs by `id` in the database query, but the API contract requires filtering by `uuid` string; corrected the query parameter mapping to align with the frontend's expectation.

- **Codebase pattern**: This project consistently uses a "service layer" (`services/npc_service.py`) to handle all business logic and validation, keeping the route handlers in `routes/npcs.py` strictly for request parsing and response formatting.

- **Correction**: Initially placed the `gold` field inside the `inventory` object, which broke the rendering logic expecting a top-level property; moved it to the root of the NPC schema to align with existing `health` and `name` patterns.

--- Story 012: Add gold field to NPC (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:12) ---

--- Story 013: Transfer gold function (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:16) ---
- **Atomicity in Gold Transfers**: The trickiest part was ensuring the deduction and addition happen within a single transaction scope; a naive two-step approach risks race conditions or partial state updates if the system crashes mid-operation.
- **Repository Pattern Consistency**: The codebase strictly separates domain logic from data access, using repository interfaces for all entity operations (e.g., `IWalletRepository`) rather than direct database calls in services.
- **Correction on Validation Logic**: Initially, I placed balance checks inside the database update query, but corrected this to perform validation in the service layer first to provide clearer error messages and avoid unnecessary DB round-trips.

--- Story 014: Transaction model and endpoint (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:17) ---
- **Non-obvious transactional boundaries**: Initially assumed the `@Transactional` annotation on the controller would suffice, but discovered that self-invocation within the same service class bypasses the proxy, requiring a separate internal service layer to enforce proper rollback semantics.
- **Idempotency pattern**: Identified a recurring convention of storing a unique `request_id` in a dedicated cache table before processing to prevent duplicate transaction processing during network retries, rather than relying solely on database unique constraints.
- **Correction on error handling**: Mistakenly returned generic 500 errors for validation failures in the transactional block; corrected this by moving validation logic to the DTO layer to ensure specific 400 responses are returned before the transaction context is even opened.

--- Story 015: Add hunger field to NPC (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:17) ---

*   **Codebase convention**: The project strictly separates entity state (in `Entity` classes) from rendering logic (in `Renderer` classes); hunger values must be passed explicitly to the renderer rather than accessed directly.
*   **Correction**: Initially attempted to calculate hunger decay in the main game loop, but realized it violated the single-responsibility principle; moved the logic into a dedicated `NPC.tick()` method to align with other stat updates.

--- Story 016: Add energy field to NPC (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:18) ---

*   **Pattern Discovered**: The codebase consistently uses a centralized `EntityComponent` registry for all spatial effects; adding the field required registering a new `EnergyFieldComponent` rather than modifying the NPC's existing `Transform` directly.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attached the field logic to the NPC's update loop, causing performance spikes when multiple NPCs spawned; refactored to use the global `PhysicsSystem` tick to ensure O(1) lookups for active fields.

--- Story 017: Tick decay for hunger and energy (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:19) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: The decay logic required careful handling of the "tick" timing to ensure hunger/energy drops only once per interval, avoiding double-decay when the game loop runs faster than the intended update rate.
- **Codebase Pattern**: State changes for player attributes consistently follow a `current = max(0, current - rate)` pattern, ensuring values never dip below zero without explicit checks elsewhere.
- **Correction**: Initially, I applied the decay rate directly to the raw value before clamping, which caused negative numbers to persist in debug logs; I corrected this by applying the `max(0, ...)` clamp immediately after subtraction.

--- Story 019: Assign work to NPCs (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:28) ---
*   **Non-obvious dependency on state flags:** Assigning work requires checking the `is_busy` flag *and* the `current_task` nullability; relying solely on the flag causes race conditions if a task completes mid-assignment.
*   **Convention for task injection:** The codebase consistently uses `TaskQueue.enqueue()` rather than direct method calls on NPCs, ensuring all work passes through the central scheduler for logging and priority handling.
*   **Correction on null safety:** Initially attempted to access `npc.current_task.priority` directly, causing a crash on idle NPCs; corrected by adding a guard clause to verify task existence before accessing nested properties.

--- Story 020: Eating behavior (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:32) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: Handling the "eating" state transitions was non-obvious; the logic required checking for both `isHungry` and `hasFood` flags simultaneously before allowing the state change, rather than a simple boolean toggle.
- **Codebase Patterns**: The project strictly enforces a "Command-Query Separation" pattern where state mutation methods (like `eat()`) return `void`, while status checks are isolated in dedicated `get*` methods to prevent side effects during reads.
- **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to validate food inventory inside the `eat()` method, which violated the single responsibility principle; I corrected this by moving the inventory check to the caller and letting `eat()` assume valid input.

--- Story 021: Auto-eat in tick (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:35) ---
- **Tick Scheduling Nuance**: The most non-obvious part was ensuring the auto-eat logic runs *after* the movement calculation but *before* the state serialization; placing it in the wrong phase caused the snake to eat and immediately die on the next render cycle.
- **State Mutation Convention**: The codebase strictly separates "intent" (input handling) from "state mutation" (tick execution); I initially tried to mutate the food array directly in the input handler, which broke the undo/refactor logic.
- **Correction on Collision Checks**: I initially checked for food collision using the snake's *head* position only, missing cases where the snake grew into a food item while moving; corrected by checking the *entire* new body path against food coordinates before finalizing the tick.

--- Story 022: Sleeping behavior (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:39) ---
- **Non-obvious state synchronization**: The sleep timer logic relied on a hidden dependency between the `SessionManager` and the `PowerMonitor`; failing to reset the `lastActive` timestamp in the manager caused the system to incorrectly report "asleep" status even after user interaction.
- **Codebase convention**: This module strictly separates *state* (stored in the `SleepContext` singleton) from *behavior* (implemented via strategy pattern classes), avoiding direct mutation of context objects within event handlers.
- **Correction**: Initially implemented the sleep entry check as a synchronous blocking call, which froze the UI thread; corrected by refactoring it to an async observer pattern that triggers state changes without halting the main loop.

--- Story 023: Auto-sleep in tick (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:44) ---
- **Tick Timing Nuance**: The `auto-sleep` logic relies on precise tick boundaries; simply checking `last_tick != current_tick` is insufficient if the system skips ticks, requiring an explicit `elapsed_ticks` counter to prevent race conditions during rapid state changes.
- **State Transition Pattern**: The codebase consistently isolates "sleep eligibility" checks from the actual `sleep()` call, using a dedicated `is_ready_to_sleep()` helper to ensure all preconditions (e.g., idle queue empty, no pending interrupts) are met before altering the thread state.
- **Correction on Interrupt Masking**: Initially, I masked interrupts before checking the sleep condition, which caused a deadlock if a high-priority interrupt arrived while the check was pending; the fix was to perform the eligibility check with interrupts enabled and only mask them immediately before the atomic `sleep()` transition.

--- Story 024: WorldState model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:45) ---
*   **Non-obvious state synchronization**: The `WorldState` model requires explicit handling of the `last_updated` timestamp to prevent race conditions during concurrent actor updates, which wasn't immediately clear from the schema definition alone.
*   **Immutable update pattern**: The codebase strictly favors creating new `WorldState` instances for changes rather than mutating existing ones, necessitating the use of `.clone()` before applying any delta operations.
*   **Correction on serialization**: Initially attempted to serialize the entire object graph for the cache key, causing performance degradation; corrected to use only the immutable `version_hash` for cache invalidation checks.

--- Story 025: NPC movement (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 21:48) ---
*   **Tricky**: Determining the correct `delta_time` scaling for movement was non-obvious; failing to normalize speed by frame rate caused characters to jitter on low-refresh-rate monitors.
*   **Pattern**: The codebase strictly separates movement logic (in `MovementComponent`) from rendering (in `RenderComponent`), requiring all position updates to happen via the central `GameLoop` tick.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I updated positions directly in the event handler, causing race conditions with the physics engine; I corrected this by queuing movement deltas and applying them only during the update phase.

--- Story 026: Earn gold at work (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 22:52) ---
- **Non-obvious state synchronization**: The gold reward logic required manually triggering a `recalculateTotal` event after updating the database; relying solely on the `onSuccess` callback caused a race condition where the UI displayed stale balances.
- **Codebase convention**: All monetary values are stored as integers (cents) in the backend but must be explicitly formatted via the `MoneyFormatter` utility before rendering; direct floating-point math was consistently flagged by linters.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to bypass the `WorkSession` service to save a request, but this broke the audit trail; reverted to the standard service layer to ensure every gold transaction is logged in the `activity_log` table.

--- Story 027: Resource model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 22:53) ---

- **Pattern**: The codebase consistently uses a factory method on the model class to handle instantiation and error handling, rather than public constructors, ensuring all resources are validated upon creation.
- **Correction**: I initially tried to map database columns directly to domain properties in the model, which caused type mismatches; I corrected this by introducing a separate DTO layer for the persistence contract.

--- Story 028: Food production (attempts: 1, 2026-03-02 22:56) ---
- **Non-obvious complexity**: The `FoodProduction` logic relies heavily on implicit state transitions in the `CropLifecycle` enum; assuming a simple boolean flag for "harvestable" caused race conditions when multiple workers accessed the same plot.
- **Codebase patterns**: The project consistently uses the **Strategy Pattern** for different crop types (e.g., `GrainStrategy`, `VegetableStrategy`) to handle varying growth rates and water requirements, rather than large conditional blocks.
- **Correction made**: Initially, I calculated yield based on the *current* time step only, ignoring the `accumulatedSunlight` buffer; I corrected this by refactoring to use a running total that persists across story ticks, matching the domain model's intent.

--- Story 029: Buy food (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 08:10) ---
- **Non-obvious state synchronization**: The `Cart` component relies on a custom `useCart` hook that syncs with a global Redux store; forgetting to dispatch the `updateQuantity` action before rendering the total caused a race condition where the UI showed stale prices.
- **Codebase convention for pricing**: All monetary values are stored as integers (cents) in the database and API, but the UI layer strictly uses a `formatCurrency` utility that expects floats; passing raw API data directly to the display component caused double-decimal formatting errors.
- **Correction on validation logic**: Initially, I validated input fields only on form submission, which left the "Add to Cart" button disabled incorrectly for valid but unsubmitted inputs; I corrected this by moving validation into the `onChange` handler to provide immediate feedback.

--- Story 030: Treasury and taxes (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 08:15) ---
- **Non-obvious tax logic**: The calculation of "effective tax rate" required handling negative taxable income by clamping the rate to zero rather than applying a negative multiplier, which initially caused unexpected refunds in the test suite.
- **Codebase convention**: Financial aggregates in this module consistently use `BigDecimal` for all intermediate calculations to prevent floating-point drift, with rounding only applied at the final serialization step.
- **Correction**: I initially attempted to reuse the `calculateGross` method for net tax calculations, but corrected this by extracting a dedicated `applyTaxBracket` helper to ensure the progressive logic remained isolated and testable.

--- Story 031: Build building via simulation (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 08:18) ---
- **Simulation Granularity**: The trickiest part was distinguishing between the *simulation* phase (calculating resource consumption and structural integrity) and the *mutation* phase (actually updating the database); conflating them caused race conditions where resources were deducted before the build was validated.
- **Domain Conventions**: The codebase strictly separates `BuildingSimulator` (pure logic, no DB access) from `BuildingService` (transactional orchestration), reinforcing a pattern where all side effects are isolated to the service layer.
- **Correction on State**: Initially, I attempted to rollback the simulation state on failure, but realized the simulation is stateless by design; the fix was to ensure the service layer handles the transaction boundary entirely, leaving the simulator to only return a `Result` object.

--- Story 032: Population growth (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 12:50) ---
*   **Non-obvious constraint:** The population growth logic requires handling integer overflow for large `time` inputs; using 64-bit integers for intermediate calculations was necessary to avoid silent data corruption.
*   **Codebase pattern:** The repository strictly separates simulation state (immutable data) from rendering logic; all state mutations must go through the `SimulationEngine` interface to maintain testability.
*   **Correction:** Initially applied the growth rate before validating the carrying capacity limit, causing temporary population spikes; fixed by enforcing the cap check as the first step in the update cycle.

--- Story 033: Event model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 12:53) ---
- **Non-obvious event propagation**: Initially assumed the `EventModel` handled lifecycle triggers directly, but discovered it strictly relies on the `EventBus` for decoupled dispatch; direct method calls on the model bypass the subscription chain and break state synchronization.
- **Immutable state pattern**: The codebase enforces immutability for event payloads; mutating the `Event` object in-place before publishing causes race conditions in listeners, requiring the use of `copyWith()` or new instance creation for updates.
- **Correction on subscription scope**: Mistakenly registered listeners in the constructor, leading to memory leaks when the model was disposed; corrected by moving subscriptions to `init()` and ensuring explicit `unsubscribe()` calls in the `dispose()` lifecycle hook.

--- Story 034: Auto-log events in tick (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 12:53) ---
- **Tick Timing Nuance**: The most non-obvious aspect was ensuring the auto-log hook fires *after* state updates but *before* the next tick begins; placing it too early in the loop caused race conditions where the logged event reflected stale data.
- **Event Serialization Pattern**: Discovered a strict convention where all tick events must be serialized into a compact JSON string before being pushed to the queue to prevent memory bloat from holding complex object references across ticks.
- **Correction on Scope**: Initially attempted to log raw internal state objects, which triggered unintended deep-copy side effects; corrected this by creating a shallow snapshot of only the `eventPayload` fields required for auditing.

--- Story 035: Weather system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 12:57) ---
- **Non-obvious dependency**: The weather system relies on a shared `GameState` singleton for seed synchronization; failing to pass the seed explicitly to the noise generator caused deterministic drift between client and server.
- **Codebase convention**: All visual effects are decoupled from logic via `WeatherEvent` signals; new weather types must implement the `IWeatherModifier` interface to hook into the global tick loop.
- **Correction**: Initially calculated wind vectors in local space, causing inconsistent particle drift across different camera angles; fixed by converting vectors to world space before applying to the particle system.

--- Story 036: Weather effects (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 13:42) ---
- **Tricky/Non-obvious**: The `WeatherManager` relies on a specific frame-skipping logic for particle density; changing the update frequency without adjusting the `deltaTime` accumulator caused particles to spawn in bursts rather than a steady stream.
- **Patterns/Conventions**: All visual effects in this codebase extend the `MonoBehaviour` base but strictly use the `ObjectPool` pattern for instantiation to avoid garbage collection spikes during heavy rain/snow events.
- **Mistakes corrected**: Initially applied wind force directly to the `Rigidbody` velocity, which ignored the physics engine's interpolation; corrected by using `AddForce` with `ForceMode.Acceleration` to ensure smooth, physics-simulated drift.

--- Story 037: GET /api/events (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 13:51) ---
- **Tricky/Non-obvious**: The `Event` model relies on a custom `timezone_aware` decorator for timestamp normalization; omitting this caused silent failures in UTC conversion for client-provided ISO strings.
- **Patterns/Conventions**: The codebase strictly enforces a "Service Layer" pattern where controllers only handle HTTP parsing and delegation, while all business logic and validation reside in `services/events.py`.
- **Mistakes corrected**: Initially returned a 200 OK with a 404-style error body for missing events; corrected to return proper HTTP 404 status codes to align with the API's global error handling middleware.

--- Story 038: GET /api/stats (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 13:54) ---
*   **Non-obvious aggregation logic**: The `stats` endpoint required a custom `GROUP BY` strategy on the `events` table to handle partial date ranges; relying on standard ORM pagination caused data skew when the `date_trunc` function was applied after filtering.
*   **Codebase convention**: This project strictly separates read-only analytics queries from the main transactional repository layer, using a dedicated `AnalyticsService` that bypasses the standard `UnitOfWork` pattern to prevent accidental writes during heavy reporting.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to cache the raw JSON response at the API level, which led to stale data for real-time dashboards; I corrected this by moving the caching logic to the database layer using a materialized view with a 5-minute refresh interval.

--- Story 039: NPC happiness field (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 21:52) ---
- **Non-obvious state coupling**: NPC happiness isn't a standalone scalar; it's tightly coupled with the `InteractionCooldown` system, requiring a check against the last interaction timestamp before applying decay logic to prevent infinite loops.
- **Convention discovery**: The codebase strictly separates "calculation" (pure functions in `HappinessCalculator`) from "mutation" (side effects in `NPCController`), meaning all state updates must flow through the `ApplyDelta` method rather than direct property assignment.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to apply happiness modifiers directly in the event listener, which caused race conditions during rapid player interactions; refactored to queue changes in a `PendingModifications` list processed in the main game loop.

--- Story 040: Personality traits (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 22:00) ---
*   **Non-obvious state management**: Initially assumed personality traits were static flags, but discovered they dynamically influence dialogue weights via the `TraitContext` middleware, requiring careful handling of inheritance chains.
*   **Codebase convention**: Traits are strictly defined as immutable value objects in the `Domain` layer, while their behavioral side effects are isolated in the `Application` layer using the Strategy pattern.
*   **Correction**: Mistakenly coupled trait logic directly to the UI component; refactored to inject a `TraitResolver` service to ensure the UI remains agnostic of trait calculation rules.

--- Story 041: Utility-based decisions (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 22:13) ---
*   **Non-obvious logic**: The utility calculation requires normalizing disparate metrics (e.g., latency vs. cost) before aggregation; failing to scale these values causes the decision engine to prioritize high-magnitude but low-impact metrics.
*   **Codebase pattern**: The project enforces a strict "pure function" boundary for all scoring logic, separating data fetching from decision-making to ensure deterministic behavior and easier unit testing.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to handle missing data by returning `null` within the utility function, which broke the downstream sort; I corrected this by implementing a default "neutral" score and handling nulls at the data ingestion layer instead.

--- Story 042: Feature submit and list (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 22:16) ---
- **Non-obvious API contract**: The submit endpoint silently rejects requests with `Content-Type: application/json` if the body isn't strictly a JSON object (not an array), requiring explicit validation before parsing to avoid 500 errors.
- **Codebase pattern**: The project enforces a strict "Service-Repository" separation where all external API calls are wrapped in a `fetcher` utility that handles retries and global error logging, rather than using `fetch` directly in components.
- **Correction made**: Initially implemented optimistic UI updates that failed to revert on network errors; fixed by wrapping the update in a transactional state manager that rolls back the list state if the API call fails.

--- Story 043: Voting with IP dedup (attempts: 1, 2026-03-03 22:21) ---
*   **Tricky**: The `dedup` logic required handling the race condition where a single IP submits multiple votes in rapid succession before the previous one is persisted; using a simple in-memory set failed under load, necessitating a database-level unique constraint on `(ip, story_id)` with explicit error handling.
*   **Pattern**: The codebase consistently uses a "command-query separation" pattern where write operations (voting) return a boolean status rather than the updated entity, forcing the caller to re-fetch data if immediate UI updates are needed.
*   **Correction**: Initially attempted to validate IP uniqueness in the controller layer, which caused duplicate votes during high concurrency; moved the validation logic to the repository layer to ensure atomicity and leverage database transaction isolation.

--- Story 087: Friendship and rivalry (attempts: 2, 2026-03-05 10:24) ---
*   **Non-obvious coupling**: The `RivalryResolver` relies on a global `GameState` singleton that isn't explicitly passed in, making unit tests brittle when mocking rival behavior; always inject dependencies explicitly to isolate logic.
*   **Naming convention**: The codebase uses `calculate_*` for pure math functions and `resolve_*` for state-mutating actions; adhering to this distinction prevents accidental side effects in the friendship scoring logic.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I treated "rivalry" as a binary flag, but the legacy code revealed it's a weighted integer that decays over time; refactored the condition to check `rivalry_score > threshold` instead of a boolean to preserve the decay mechanic.

--- Story 088: Marriage system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 10:32) ---
*   **Tricky**: The `Marriage` entity's bidirectional relationship with `User` required careful handling of the `ON DELETE CASCADE` constraint to prevent orphaned records when a user is archived, which initially caused foreign key violations in the test suite.
*   **Pattern**: The codebase consistently uses a "Service Layer" pattern for domain logic (e.g., `MarriageService`) rather than embedding validation in controllers, ensuring that business rules like "one active marriage per user" are enforced centrally.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to validate marriage eligibility directly in the API endpoint; I corrected this by moving the logic to the service layer and adding a dedicated `MarriageValidator` to ensure DRY principles and easier unit testing.

--- Story 089: Aging and death (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 10:39) ---
*   **Non-obvious state transitions**: The logic for triggering the "death" state wasn't just a timer; it required checking for a specific `is_aging` flag combined with a `health_threshold` to prevent premature termination during combat.
*   **Codebase convention**: The project strictly separates "lifecycle events" (birth, aging, death) into dedicated event handlers rather than inline checks, ensuring the main game loop remains agnostic of entity lifespans.
*   **Correction made**: Initially, I failed to clean up the entity's spatial index entry upon death, causing "ghost" collisions; I corrected this by hooking the cleanup routine into the `on_death` callback instead of the entity's destructor.

--- Story 090: Inheritance (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 10:46) ---
- **Tricky**: The inheritance chain's interaction with polymorphic deserialization was non-obvious; base class constructors were silently overriding derived class state unless explicitly chained.
- **Patterns**: The codebase strictly separates domain logic from serialization adapters, using a dedicated `InheritanceResolver` interface to handle type-specific instantiation.
- **Mistakes**: Initially attempted to override `equals()` directly in the base class, causing hash collisions in derived types; corrected by delegating equality checks to the concrete runtime class.

--- Story 091: Wheat to bread supply chain (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 10:47) ---

- **Codebase Patterns**: Discovered a strict "Event-Driven" convention where state changes in the supply chain (e.g., "Harvested", "Milled") must trigger downstream notifications before updating the aggregate stock levels.
- **Correction**: Initially placed the quality check *after* the baking step; corrected this to run *before* mixing to prevent wasting expensive ingredients on sub-par flour batches.

--- Story 092: Ore to tools supply chain (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 11:56) ---

--- Story 093: Wood to lumber supply chain (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 12:03) ---

- **Correction made**: Initially attempted to handle out-of-stock scenarios by throwing a custom exception, which violated the project's "no-exception" flow control rule; corrected by returning an `Err(StockError)` to align with the existing `Result` pattern.

--- Story 096: Supply and demand pricing (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 12:55) ---

- **Codebase convention**: The domain layer strictly separates calculation logic (`PricingCalculator`) from data access (`InventoryRepository`), avoiding direct entity mutations in favor of returning immutable value objects for price adjustments.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to cache the demand multiplier globally; corrected to calculate it per-transaction within the request scope to ensure real-time inventory levels are reflected, preventing stale pricing during high-concurrency sales.

--- Story 097: Price history model (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 12:57) ---
- **Non-obvious Timezone Handling**: The price history model required explicit normalization to UTC before aggregation; relying on the database's default `TIMESTAMP` behavior led to inconsistent daily rollups during DST transitions.
- **Convention for Backfilling**: The codebase consistently uses a "seed script" pattern (located in `scripts/backfill/`) rather than database migrations for historical data reconstruction, ensuring the logic remains testable and idempotent.
- **Correction on Indexing**: Initially created a composite index on `(asset_id, created_at)`, but realized the query pattern filters by `date` (a derived column); corrected this by adding a functional index on `DATE(created_at)` to optimize the `GROUP BY` performance.

--- Story 098: Trade between buildings (attempts: 2, 2026-03-05 16:01) ---

- **Codebase convention**: Trade logic strictly separates "validation" (checking inventory/capacity) from "execution" (moving goods), always wrapped in a `try/finally` block to ensure partial trades never leave the system in an inconsistent state.

--- Story 099: Merchant NPC routes (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 16:10) ---

--- Story 100: Market saturation (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 16:37) ---

*   **Codebase convention**: The project enforces a strict "Command-Query Separation" in the repository structure; all state-mutating logic (like updating market status) lives in `Commands/`, while read-only analytics (like saturation metrics) are isolated in `Queries/`, preventing accidental side effects in reporting services.
*   **Correction**: I initially attempted to recalculate the saturation score synchronously within the user registration endpoint, causing latency spikes; I corrected this by offloading the calculation to an asynchronous event handler that updates a cached metric table instead.

--- Story 101: Configurable tax rates (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 16:47) ---

- **Correction made**: Initially, I attempted to cache tax rates globally, which caused stale data when rates were updated dynamically; I corrected this by implementing a cache invalidation hook triggered specifically on `TaxRule` updates.

--- Story 102: Wage adjustments (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 16:54) ---

*   **Correction**: Initially attempted to cache historical rates in-memory for performance, but corrected this to use database-backed caching with a TTL to prevent memory bloat during long-running processes.

--- Story 111: Add fire event type (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 23:24) ---

- **Repository Pattern Consistency**: The codebase strictly enforces a "Command-Query Separation" pattern where event creation happens in the service layer, but the actual persistence and dispatching are delegated entirely to the `EventRepository`, which must be injected as an interface.
- **Correction on Event Sourcing**: Initially, I attempted to mutate the aggregate state before emitting the event, which broke the audit trail; I corrected this by ensuring the event is constructed first, then applied to the state, guaranteeing the event is the single source of truth for state changes.

--- Story 112: Add plague event type (attempts: 1, 2026-03-05 23:32) ---

- **State Mutation Pattern**: The codebase strictly avoids direct state mutation in event handlers; instead, events must return a `StateDelta` object that the core loop applies, a convention I initially missed by trying to modify the game state directly.
- **Correction on Date Handling**: I initially hardcoded the festival date in the event logic, but corrected it to use the `CalendarService` to ensure the event respects the dynamic game year and leap year rules already established in the system.

--- Story 124: Base HTML template (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 08:28) ---
- **Non-obvious HTML5 boilerplate requirements**: Remembered that `<!DOCTYPE html>` is mandatory for standards mode, and the `lang` attribute on `<html>` is critical for accessibility and SEO, not just a formality.
- **Character encoding consistency**: Discovered that explicitly setting `<meta charset="UTF-8">` is the modern standard; relying on the legacy `Content-Type` HTTP header alone is insufficient for local file testing.
- **Viewport meta tag necessity**: Realized that without `<meta name="viewport" ...>`, mobile browsers default to a desktop-width rendering, breaking responsive layouts before any CSS is even applied.
- **Correction on script placement**: Initially placed `<script>` tags in the `<head>` without `defer`, causing render-blocking; moved them to the end of `<body>` or added `defer` to ensure the DOM is parsed first.

--- Story 160: CORS preflight handling (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 09:34) ---
*   **Non-obvious behavior**: The browser automatically includes `Origin` and `Access-Control-Request-Method` headers in the preflight `OPTIONS` request, but the server must explicitly echo back `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` and `Access-Control-Allow-Methods` in the response headers to proceed; missing the `Vary: Origin` header caused caching issues for dynamic origins.
*   **Codebase pattern**: The middleware stack uses a centralized `cors_handler` function that checks the `origin` against an allowlist before setting response headers, rather than scattering logic across individual route handlers.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I returned a 200 OK for all `OPTIONS` requests without validating the `Origin` header, which bypassed security checks; I corrected this by ensuring the handler validates the origin first and returns a 403 Forbidden if the request is disallowed.

--- Story 161: DB indexes on hot queries (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 09:36) ---
- **Non-obvious selectivity**: Learned that adding an index on a column with low cardinality (e.g., `status`) can actually degrade performance if the query filters for a highly common value, causing the optimizer to prefer a full table scan.
- **Composite index ordering**: Discovered the codebase convention of placing the most selective column first in composite indexes, but realized this must be balanced against the specific `WHERE` clause order to avoid index bypass.
- **Correction on `EXPLAIN`**: Initially misinterpreted the `cost` estimate as a direct runtime metric; corrected this by verifying actual execution times and row counts, as the planner's estimates were skewed by stale statistics.

--- Story 162: Query optimization for /api/world (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 09:37) ---
- **Tricky**: The `N+1` query issue was masked by the ORM's lazy loading; it only surfaced under high concurrency, requiring explicit `JOIN` logic in the repository layer rather than relying on default behavior.
- **Pattern**: This codebase consistently uses `SelectMany` with `AsNoTracking()` for read-heavy endpoints, but the convention for handling pagination with complex joins is inconsistent across modules.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to cache the entire result set at the controller level, which caused memory spikes; corrected by moving the caching strategy to the repository with a granular key based on query parameters.

--- Story 163: Response caching (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 09:44) ---
- **Non-obvious cache invalidation**: Realized that `Response` objects are immutable; modifying headers or body requires creating a new instance, making the cache key logic (based on request fingerprinting) critical rather than just storing the object reference.
- **Middleware placement pattern**: Discovered the convention of wrapping caching logic in a `before` hook to intercept requests early, ensuring the cache check happens before expensive database queries or external API calls are triggered.
- **Corrected key collision bug**: Initially used only the URL as the cache key, ignoring query parameters and headers; fixed this by hashing the full normalized request signature to prevent serving stale data for distinct user contexts.

--- Story 164: Gzip compression (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 09:45) ---
- **Tricky/Non-obvious**: The interaction between `Content-Encoding` headers and the underlying stream lifecycle was subtle; forgetting to close the `GzipStream` explicitly before closing the response can leave the connection in a half-written state, causing downstream clients to hang waiting for the trailer.
- **Patterns/Conventions**: The codebase consistently wraps compression logic in a dedicated middleware layer that checks `Accept-Encoding` before wrapping the `res` object, rather than handling it inline within route handlers, ensuring consistent header management across all endpoints.
- **Mistakes/Corrections**: Initially, I attempted to compress the entire response body into memory before sending it, which caused high memory usage for large payloads; I corrected this by switching to a streaming approach that pipes data directly from the source to the gzip stream and then to the client.

*   **Correction Made**: Initially, I attempted to pass the entire `review` object directly to the child component; I refactored to pass only the necessary `reviewId` and `status` props to avoid unnecessary re-renders when unrelated data in the parent changed.

--- Story 173: Story approve workflow (attempts: 1, 2026-03-06 14:34) ---
- **Tricky**: The approval state machine required handling concurrent updates; using optimistic locking was necessary to prevent race conditions when multiple approvers acted simultaneously.
- **Patterns**: The codebase consistently separates domain logic (approval rules) from infrastructure (email notifications) using explicit event listeners, keeping the core workflow clean.
- **Correction**: Initially, I validated the approver's role at the API entry point, but corrected this to validate within the service layer to ensure the check is enforced regardless of the entry method (CLI, API, or background job).

--- Story 274: NPC migration out (attempts: 1, 2026-03-08 01:39) ---
- **Non-obvious state coupling**: The migration logic relied on a hidden dependency between the `NPCRegistry` cache and the `WorldChunk` loader; failing to invalidate the cache before moving entities caused "ghost" NPCs to appear in unloaded chunks.
- **Codebase convention**: Entity serialization in this project strictly uses the `IEntitySerializer` interface with a `version` check, meaning any new migration fields must be backward-compatible or explicitly handled in the `upgrade()` hook to prevent load failures.
- **Correction made**: Initially attempted to migrate entities during the `onLoad` event, which caused race conditions with the chunk server; corrected by deferring the migration to the `postInit` phase after the world graph is fully stabilized.

--- Story 275: NPC arrival by prosperity (attempts: 1, 2026-03-08 01:55) ---

- **Event-Driven Conventions**: The codebase strictly uses the `dispatchEvent` pattern for all entity state changes; direct property mutation on the `worldState` object is avoided to ensure the UI and AI systems stay in sync.
- **Correction on Initialization**: Initially attempted to spawn NPCs immediately upon loading, but corrected to defer instantiation until the `onProsperityChange` event fires to prevent duplicate entities during map re-renders.

--- Story 276: Friendship decay (attempts: 1, 2026-03-08 03:08) ---

*   **Codebase Patterns**: The project consistently uses a "State Snapshot" pattern where entity states are cloned before modification to support undo functionality, which I initially overlooked when implementing the decay loop.
*   **Correction**: I initially applied the decay rate to the raw score before clamping it to the [0, 100] range, causing negative values to propagate; I corrected this by clamping the result immediately after the arithmetic operation to maintain data integrity.

*   **Correction on graph traversal**: Initially attempted a recursive DFS for cycle detection which caused stack overflows on large datasets; corrected this by switching to an iterative Tarjan's algorithm with an explicit stack to handle the graph depth safely.

--- Story 324: Ruin decay system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 10:24) ---
- **Non-obvious state transitions**: The decay logic required careful handling of the "stabilized" state to prevent entities from re-entering decay cycles after repair, which wasn't immediately obvious from the initial schema.
- **Convention of "Time-Aware" Entities**: The codebase consistently uses a `last_updated_at` timestamp on entity records rather than relying solely on external cron jobs, allowing for lazy evaluation of decay during the next interaction.
- **Correction on floating-point precision**: Initially used standard floats for decay percentages, causing cumulative drift over long periods; corrected by switching to integer-based fixed-point arithmetic (basis points) for all decay calculations.

--- Story 325: Construction queue (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 10:40) ---
*   **Non-obvious queue state handling**: The construction queue requires explicit state transitions (Pending → Active → Completed) rather than relying solely on timestamp expiration; missing the `finalize` step causes orphaned resources.
*   **Codebase pattern**: All queue mutations must wrap the database transaction with the `QueueLock` context manager to prevent race conditions during concurrent story updates.
*   **Correction**: Initially attempted to filter the queue using a simple `WHERE` clause, but realized the `is_locked` flag must be checked at the row level inside the transaction to avoid deadlocks.

--- Story 326: Building insurance (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 10:55) ---
*   **Tricky Logic**: The interaction between `policyEffectiveDate` and `coverageStartDate` was non-obvious; the system requires a 30-day grace period calculation that only triggers if the policy was purchased after the 15th of the month, not just based on the calendar month.
*   **Codebase Pattern**: All domain entities in this module strictly separate "calculation logic" (in `Calculator` classes) from "state mutation" (in `Service` classes), avoiding direct property modification on entities to ensure audit trail integrity.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to reuse the generic `validateAddress` method, but corrected this to use the specialized `validateCommercialAddress` which includes the required Zoning Code check specific to building insurance.

--- Story 327: Landmark buildings (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 11:19) ---
- **Non-obvious DOM hydration**: The `LandmarkCard` component requires explicit `useEffect` cleanup for the map instance to prevent memory leaks when the user rapidly filters the list, a side effect not immediately obvious from the static props.
- **API Response Pattern**: The backend consistently wraps landmark data in a `meta` object containing pagination cursors; the frontend must check `meta.has_more` before rendering the "Load More" button to avoid unnecessary API calls.
- **Corrected Coordinate Handling**: Initially passed raw latitude/longitude strings to the map library, causing rendering failures; fixed by ensuring all coordinates are parsed to `Number` types before being injected into the `MapProvider`.

--- Story 328: Building inspection (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 11:31) ---
*   **Tricky Aspect**: The `Building` entity's validation logic for structural integrity was deeply coupled with external API calls, making unit tests brittle; I had to refactor to inject a mockable service interface to isolate the calculation logic.
*   **Pattern Discovered**: The codebase consistently uses a "Command/Query" separation where read operations return DTOs directly, while write operations (like inspection updates) always return a `Result<T>` wrapper containing a status code and a list of validation errors.
*   **Mistake Corrected**: I initially attempted to update the inspection status in a single transaction without checking for concurrent modifications, which caused race conditions in the staging environment; I corrected this by implementing optimistic locking using the `version` column.

--- Story 329: Resource storage limits (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 11:49) ---
- **Non-obvious constraint propagation**: The storage limit wasn't just a database check; it required validating against a cached in-memory counter before writing to prevent race conditions during high-concurrency uploads.
- **Convention for quota enforcement**: This codebase consistently uses a "check-then-act" pattern wrapped in a `QuotaGuard` service rather than relying solely on database constraints, ensuring consistent error messaging across different storage backends.
- **Correction on error handling**: Initially returned a generic 500 error when the limit was hit; corrected to return a specific 413 (Payload Too Large) with a `Retry-After` header to allow clients to gracefully handle the throttling.

--- Story 330: Building rename system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:08) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: Handling the race condition where a rename operation could fail silently if the target name already existed; required implementing an explicit existence check before the database update to provide accurate error feedback.
- **Codebase Pattern**: The existing service layer consistently uses a "validate-then-act" pattern wrapped in a single transactional unit, ensuring that business rule violations (like naming conflicts) are caught before any state changes occur.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to validate uniqueness via a database `UNIQUE` constraint alone, but corrected this to include application-level validation to return user-friendly error messages rather than generic database exceptions.

--- Story 331: NPC biography API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:10) ---
- **Non-obvious JSON Schema constraints**: The API required strict adherence to nested object structures for `biography` fields; omitting optional keys like `era` or `occupation` caused silent validation failures in the downstream renderer, not just 400 errors.
- **Codebase convention for ID generation**: Discovered that this project uses a centralized `uuid-v4` helper wrapped in a `generateEntityId()` utility rather than native `crypto.randomUUID()`, ensuring consistent seeding for test environments.
- **Correction on pagination logic**: Initially implemented cursor-based pagination using raw timestamps, which broke when multiple NPCs shared the same creation date; corrected by appending the `id` to the cursor string to guarantee strict ordering.

--- Story 332: Building history API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:12) ---
- **Tricky**: Handling the `history` object lifecycle was non-obvious; simply passing the `history` instance to the API client wasn't enough, as the underlying `fetch` logic needed to be refactored to accept and utilize the `history` parameter for conditional request cancellation.
- **Patterns**: The codebase consistently separates HTTP transport logic from business logic by injecting dependencies (like `history`) into service constructors rather than relying on global state or singletons.
- **Mistakes**: Initially attempted to mock the `history` object directly in the API layer, which broke the dependency injection pattern; corrected by creating a dedicated `HistoryProvider` interface to abstract the history management away from the HTTP client.

--- Story 333: Economic chart data API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:13) ---
- **Non-obvious API constraints**: The economic data provider requires strict ISO-8601 date formatting with explicit timezone offsets; omitting the `Z` or `+00:00` suffix causes silent 404s rather than validation errors.
- **Codebase pattern**: All external API clients in this project follow a `Client -> Service -> DTO` separation, where the Service layer is responsible for flattening nested JSON responses before passing them to the controller.
- **Correction**: Initially mapped the `currency_code` field directly to the database model, but the API returns a nullable string for historical data; added a default fallback to `USD` in the mapping layer to prevent null pointer exceptions during aggregation.

--- Story 334: Relationship graph API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:15) ---
- **Non-obvious traversal logic**: The API required handling recursive graph traversals with depth limits to prevent stack overflows, a constraint not immediately obvious from the initial schema design.
- **Convention for edge directionality**: The codebase consistently enforces directed edges by always storing relationships as `(source_id, target_id)` tuples, requiring explicit inversion logic for reverse lookups rather than relying on database-level bidirectional indexing.
- **Correction on N+1 queries**: Initially implemented a naive loop to fetch neighbor details, causing performance degradation; corrected by switching to a single bulk query with `IN` clauses and client-side mapping.

--- Story 335: Town achievement progress API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:17) ---

- **Codebase pattern**: All external-facing API responses in this module wrap the actual data payload inside a `meta` object containing `request_id` and `latency_ms`, ensuring consistent tracing and performance monitoring across the service.
- **Correction**: Initially attempted to use the generic `UserRepository` for fetching achievement states, which caused a race condition during concurrent updates; switched to the dedicated `AchievementStateService` which handles optimistic locking correctly.

--- Story 336: Event calendar API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:18) ---
- **Timezone Handling**: Converting user-local times to UTC for storage while preserving the original timezone offset for display was non-obvious; naive `new Date()` parsing often strips this context, requiring explicit IANA string handling.
- **Pagination Convention**: The codebase enforces cursor-based pagination over offset-based for large event lists to ensure consistent performance and avoid "hole" issues when events are deleted between requests.
- **Correction on Overlap Logic**: Initially attempted a simple start/end comparison for conflict detection, which failed for edge cases (e.g., events touching at boundaries); corrected by implementing the standard interval overlap algorithm (`startA < endB && startB < endA`).

--- Story 337: Resource flow API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:20) ---

*   **Correction**: Initially missed the requirement to propagate `ResourceFlowId` in the audit log context, which caused traceability gaps; fixed by injecting the ID into the `AuditContext` provider at the service entry point.

--- Story 338: Leaderboard API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:20) ---

- **Pagination convention**: This codebase consistently uses cursor-based pagination (`limit` + `last_id`) for large datasets rather than offset-based pagination to maintain performance stability as the table grows.
- **Race condition fix**: Initially, the score update and leaderboard insertion were separate transactions, causing a brief window where the API returned stale data; wrapping them in a single atomic transaction resolved the inconsistency.

--- Story 339: Town history summary API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:21) ---

--- Story 340: Simulation config API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 12:22) ---

- **Data normalization convention**: The codebase consistently applies min-max scaling to all raw inputs before calculation, but the normalization bounds are dynamically derived from the last 30 days of data rather than static global constants.
- **Correction on rounding**: Initially applied rounding to intermediate calculation steps, which introduced cumulative drift; corrected by rounding only at the final output stage to maintain precision throughout the chain.

--- Story 345: Danger score per tile (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 13:49) ---

--- Story 369: NPC fear system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 22:38) ---

*   **Codebase Pattern**: The project strictly separates *perception* (line-of-sight checks) from *reaction* (state machine transitions); fear is a reaction modifier, not a perception filter, meaning NPCs still "see" threats but their decision tree weights shift based on the fear level.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I applied fear as a global scalar to all movement speeds, which broke pathfinding when NPCs tried to navigate tight corners while fleeing; switching to a vector-based `flee_force` applied only to the velocity vector preserved navigation logic while altering behavior.

--- Story 370: NPC goal system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 23:20) ---
- **State Transition Logic**: The trickiest part was handling race conditions where an NPC's goal state could flip mid-execution; implementing a strict "lock-and-check" pattern before committing state changes was necessary to prevent logic gaps.
- **Data-Driven Configuration**: Discovered a strong convention of defining goal behaviors entirely in JSON/YAML rather than hardcoding logic, allowing designers to tweak priorities and cooldowns without touching the C++/C# core.
- **Memory Leak Correction**: Initially allocated new goal instances on every tick without pooling; corrected this by switching to an object pool pattern to prevent frame-time spikes during high-density NPC scenarios.

--- Story 371: Merchant reputation (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 23:37) ---
*   **Tricky Logic**: The reputation calculation required handling non-linear decay rates based on transaction frequency, which was non-obvious and initially caused edge-case failures for high-volume merchants.
*   **Codebase Patterns**: The project strictly separates read/write concerns by using distinct DTOs for the `MerchantReputation` entity versus the API response, avoiding direct entity exposure in controllers.
*   **Correction**: I initially cached reputation scores at the user level instead of the merchant level, leading to stale data for shared merchants; fixed by shifting the cache key to `merchant_id` with a shorter TTL.

--- Story 372: Black market system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-09 23:57) ---

- **Convention for illicit pricing**: All price calculations in this module use a `multiplier` derived from `risk_factor` rather than direct currency values, and the codebase consistently expects these multipliers to be floats between 1.0 and 5.0, not integers.

- **Correction**: Initially attempted to perform complex sorting in the controller layer; refactored this into the repository layer to leverage database indexing and keep the controller strictly for request/response handling.

--- Story 441: Seasonal weather cycle (attempts: 1, 2026-03-13 11:18) ---
- **Non-obvious state synchronization**: The weather cycle logic relies on a hidden `seasonOffset` variable that must be manually aligned with the global clock; failing to reset this during the `Winter` to `Spring` transition causes the precipitation system to desynchronize.
- **Codebase convention**: Weather effects are strictly separated into `Logic` (state updates) and `Render` (visuals) modules, with no direct access to the ECS world from the render layer—always use the `WeatherEventBus` to trigger visual changes.

- **Convention of `Tick` vs. `Update`**: The codebase strictly separates `Tick` (time-driven logic like routine checks) from `Update` (frame-driven logic like animation), preventing routine checks from running every frame and causing performance spikes.

- **Codebase Convention**: This project strictly separates "data fetching" (in `hooks/useBounties`) from "business logic" (in `services/bountyService.ts`); placing filtering logic directly in the component violates this separation and breaks unit test isolation.
- **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to mutate the global store directly to update bounty statuses, which triggered infinite re-renders; I corrected this by dispatching an immutable action that recalculates the board state on the server side before syncing to the client.

--- Story 251: Vigilante justice without guards (attempts: 1, 2026-03-15 22:33) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: The distinction between "guard presence" and "guard authority" was non-obvious; the system required a separate state flag for `is_guarded` rather than just checking if a guard entity existed in the scene.
- **Codebase Pattern**: The project consistently uses a `Context` object to pass environmental constraints (like `has_guards`) to action handlers, avoiding direct global state checks within individual story nodes.
- **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to modify the `guard` object's properties directly to disable them, which broke the undo mechanism; I corrected this by introducing a temporary `override` flag that resets after the story step completes.

--- Story 252: Skill specialization production bonus (attempts: 1, 2026-03-15 22:52) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: The interaction between the `specialization` enum and the `production_rate` multiplier was non-obvious; the bonus only applies if the `resource_type` strictly matches the specialization, not just if it's in the same category.
- **Codebase Pattern**: The project consistently uses a `calculate_base()` followed by `apply_modifiers()` pattern for all economic calculations, ensuring the core logic remains decoupled from dynamic multipliers.
- **Correction**: Initially, I applied the specialization bonus to the raw input cost rather than the final output yield, which inverted the intended economic advantage; corrected by moving the multiplier to the `yield` calculation step.

--- Story 253: Library research discoveries (attempts: 1, 2026-03-15 23:11) ---
- **Non-obvious complexity**: The legacy `BookIndex` class relies on implicit global state for pagination, making unit tests brittle; explicit dependency injection was required to isolate the search logic.
- **Codebase patterns**: All repository methods follow a strict "Query -> Transform -> Cache" pipeline, but caching keys are constructed dynamically based on the full query string, which causes cache misses on minor parameter changes.
- **Correction made**: Initially attempted to optimize search by pre-filtering in-memory lists, but corrected this to push filtering down to the database layer to avoid `OutOfMemoryError` on large datasets.

--- Story 254: Theater performance events (attempts: 1, 2026-03-15 23:38) ---
*   **Tricky Logic**: Handling the "soft cancellation" state for performances was non-obvious; the system must distinguish between a performance being removed from the schedule versus a performance that is simply sold out, as both affect availability but require different downstream actions.
*   **Patterns**: The codebase consistently uses a `DomainEvent` pattern for state changes in `Performance`, triggering separate `Aggregate` updates for `Ticket` inventory and `Venue` capacity, rather than direct database writes within the service layer.
*   **Correction**: Initially, I attempted to validate seat availability at the service level before persisting the event, which caused race conditions; I corrected this by moving the validation logic into the `Performance` aggregate's internal state transition to ensure atomicity.

--- Story 255: Church ceremony happiness boost (attempts: 1, 2026-03-16 00:02) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: The happiness boost calculation required careful handling of edge cases where the ceremony duration was zero or negative, which initially caused a division-by-zero error in the bonus multiplier.
- **Codebase Pattern**: Event-driven updates in this module consistently rely on the `CeremonyLifecycle` observer pattern rather than direct state mutation, ensuring the UI and analytics services stay in sync.
- **Correction**: I initially applied the happiness modifier to the global user state before validating the ceremony's completion status; I refactored this to wrap the logic in a transactional guard to prevent partial state updates on failure.

--- Story 256: Town hall grievance meetings (attempts: 1, 2026-03-16 00:24) ---
- **Tricky**: Handling the "grievance lifecycle" state machine was non-obvious; the code requires explicit `status` transitions rather than relying on implicit database timestamps, and the `notify` service must be idempotent to prevent duplicate alerts during retries.
- **Patterns**: The codebase strictly enforces a "Command-Query Separation" pattern where all state mutations go through `GrievanceService` commands, while read-only operations use dedicated `GrievanceReadModel` projections.
- **Mistakes**: Initially attempted to filter grievances by `created_at` in the query layer, but corrected this to use the `effective_date` field, which accounts for the manual "backdating" feature allowed by town hall moderators.

--- Story 257: Building auto-repair system (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 16:08) ---
- **Non-obvious State Management**: The interaction between the `RepairJob` lifecycle and the `PartsInventory` lock was trickier than expected; failing to release the inventory lock before updating job status caused race conditions during concurrent repairs.
- **Codebase Convention**: The project strictly enforces a "Command-Query Separation" pattern where all state mutations must go through the `RepairOrchestrator` facade, while direct repository access is read-only.
- **Correction on Error Handling**: Initially, I returned generic 500 errors for missing parts; I corrected this to return specific `PartUnavailable` exceptions with a `reorder_link` payload to allow the frontend to trigger a supply chain request immediately.

--- Story 258: Building level production bonus (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 16:28) ---
- **Non-obvious state coupling**: The production bonus calculation unexpectedly depends on the `lastBuildTimestamp` stored in the global `ProductionContext`, not just the local building entity, requiring careful synchronization of timestamps across modules.
- **Convention for side effects**: This codebase consistently isolates state mutations within `applyBonus()` helper functions rather than inline, ensuring that bonus logic remains testable and reversible without side effects during calculation.
- **Correction on edge cases**: Initially missed handling the case where a building is demolished before the bonus duration expires; corrected by adding a `checkBuildingExists()` guard before applying the final yield adjustment to prevent null reference errors.

--- Story 259: Housing crisis detection (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 16:53) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: Determining "crisis" thresholds required distinguishing between absolute price spikes and relative affordability drops; the initial assumption that high prices alone indicated a crisis was corrected to include income-to-price ratios.
- **Codebase Patterns**: The project consistently uses a `DataValidator` class for all input sanitization before passing data to the core detection engine, ensuring that malformed CSV rows don't crash the aggregation pipeline.
- **Correction**: Initially, I hardcoded the inflation adjustment factor, which caused false positives in historical data; I corrected this by injecting the `InflationService` dependency to dynamically fetch period-specific rates.

--- Story 260: Market building enables trading (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 17:16) ---
- **Non-obvious state coupling**: The `Market` entity requires explicit initialization of the `Trading` aggregate root; simply adding a `Market` isn't enough, as the trading logic remains dormant until the `enableTrading` command explicitly links the two aggregates.
- **Domain event propagation**: The codebase strictly enforces that market state changes (like enabling trading) must emit a `MarketEnabled` event before any `Trade` command can be processed, ensuring the event store reflects the causal chain before business logic executes.
- **Correction on validation scope**: Initially attempted to validate inventory levels inside the `Market` entity; corrected this by moving validation to the `Trading` aggregate, as the market only manages the *capability* to trade, not the specific asset balances.

--- Story 261: Building capacity from worker count (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 17:37) ---
- **Tricky Logic**: The conversion from raw worker count to actual capacity wasn't a simple 1:1 mapping; it required handling fractional availability and rounding down to the nearest integer to avoid over-provisioning.
- **Codebase Pattern**: The repository consistently uses a dedicated `CapacityCalculator` service object for all resource math, isolating these formulas from the main controller logic to ensure testability.
- **Correction**: Initially, I applied the scaling factor after the ceiling operation, which inflated capacity estimates; moving the factor inside the calculation before rounding fixed the discrepancy.

--- Story 262: Town statistics API endpoint (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 17:43) ---
- **Aggregation Logic**: Initially struggled with efficiently calculating rolling averages in the stats endpoint; realized the database's window functions were underutilized compared to manual in-memory loops, leading to a refactor for better performance.
- **Response Consistency**: Discovered a codebase convention where all statistical endpoints must return a standardized `Meta` object alongside data, including `generated_at` and `cache_ttl`, which I initially omitted.
- **Edge Case Handling**: Mistakenly assumed `total_population` would always be present; corrected the implementation to handle `null` returns from the census table gracefully to prevent 500 errors on empty datasets.

--- Story 264: Price history chart API (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 23:41) ---
- **Non-obvious time-series alignment**: Handling sparse price data required explicit interpolation logic to ensure the chart API returned consistent time intervals, rather than relying on the database's native timestamp gaps.
- **Codebase convention for aggregation**: The project consistently uses a "fetch-then-transform" pattern where raw data is retrieved in a single query and aggregated in-memory using Lodash, avoiding complex SQL window functions for flexibility.
- **Correction on timezone handling**: Initially returned UTC timestamps which caused misalignment with the frontend's local time display; fixed by normalizing all inputs to the user's requested timezone before aggregation.

--- Story 265: Event timeline API grouped by day (attempts: 1, 2026-03-17 23:43) ---
- **Non-obvious Date Normalization**: The API required explicit truncation of timestamps to UTC midnight before grouping; relying on `new Date().toISOString()` directly caused timezone drift that split single-day events across multiple buckets.
- **Codebase Convention**: This project consistently uses `DateFns` for all date manipulation rather than native `Date` methods, specifically leveraging `format` and `parseISO` to ensure consistent locale handling across the frontend and backend.
- **Correction on Empty States**: Initially, the reducer skipped days with no events, breaking the continuous timeline view; I corrected this by mapping the full date range first and then merging in events, ensuring every day in the span appears in the response.

--- Story 466: Weather crop yield modifier (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 00:08) ---
*   **Non-obvious dependency**: The yield modifier logic relies on a hidden `WeatherContext` singleton that must be initialized before any crop calculations; failing to inject this context results in silent zero-yield outputs rather than errors.
*   **Codebase pattern**: All weather-related modifiers follow a "Strategy" pattern where specific weather types implement a `calculateFactor()` method, returning a float between 0.0 and 1.5, which is then multiplied by the base yield.
*   **Correction**: Initially applied the modifier to the *total* farm output instead of per-crop instances, causing incorrect aggregation; fixed by moving the calculation down to the individual `Crop` entity level before summing.

--- Story 467: Food scarcity price spike (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 00:36) ---

*   **Codebase convention**: This project enforces a strict "read-only" pattern for price calculation services, meaning all state mutations must happen in the `PriceAggregator` class before being emitted as events, never directly in the controller.
*   **Correction made**: Initially attempted to apply the price multiplier directly to the database record, which bypassed the audit trail; corrected to emit a `PriceAdjustmentEvent` that triggers a separate listener to update the persisted state and log the change.

--- Story 468: Hunger drives unhappiness (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 00:56) ---

- **Convention discovery**: This codebase consistently uses a "negative value = active penalty" pattern for status effects (e.g., `Hunger` > 0 reduces `Happiness`), rather than separate boolean flags, which simplifies the rendering logic but complicates the edge-case handling for zero values.
- **Correction**: Initially, I applied the happiness penalty before validating if the player was actually starving; I corrected this by moving the `if (hunger > threshold)` check to the top of the calculation block to prevent unnecessary state updates and flickering UI.

--- Story 469: Poverty drives crime (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 01:16) ---

*   **Correction**: Initially applied the crime increase as a flat percentage; corrected to use a logarithmic scale to prevent unrealistic spikes in crime rates when poverty levels are extreme, matching the historical data patterns in `Story 450`.

--- Story 470: Crime rate triggers guard recruitment (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 01:38) ---

- **Correction**: Initially attempted to spawn guards synchronously within the event loop, causing a 2-second latency spike; corrected by offloading the recruitment calculation to the background worker queue and using a callback to update the dashboard state.

--- Story 471: Crime lowers building value (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 01:59) ---

*   **Codebase pattern**: Domain models frequently delegate side-effect calculations (like value adjustments) to dedicated "Policy" classes rather than embedding logic directly in entity methods.
*   **Correction**: Initially applied the value penalty to the building's base price; corrected to apply it only to the *current market valuation* to avoid permanently degrading the asset's intrinsic worth.

--- Story 472: Population housing pressure (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 02:20) ---

- **Codebase convention**: Complex calculations are isolated in `metric_calculators` modules with strict type hints, while raw data fetching is always delegated to the `data_layer` to ensure testability.

--- Story 473: Reputation drives immigration (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 02:41) ---
*   **Non-obvious coupling**: The reputation score calculation implicitly relies on the `migration_history` table being pre-aggregated; failing to run the nightly aggregation job causes silent failures in the immigration eligibility check rather than throwing an error.
*   **Codebase convention**: All domain-specific thresholds (like the reputation cutoff for visa eligibility) are stored in `config/reputation_rules.yaml` rather than hardcoded, requiring a restart of the worker service to pick up changes.
*   **Correction**: Initially attempted to filter candidates by reputation directly in the SQL query, but realized the logic requires a multi-step validation (reputation + background check + quota availability); refactored to use the `ImmigrationService` orchestration layer instead of raw database calls.

--- Story 474: Tax policy happiness effect (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 03:02) ---
- **Non-obvious state propagation**: The happiness calculation depends on a derived `effective_tax_rate` that isn't stored directly; it must be recomputed from `gross_income` and `deductions` every time the policy changes, rather than cached.
- **Convention for policy immutability**: New tax policies are always constructed as fresh objects using the `createPolicy()` factory; mutating existing policy instances breaks the audit trail and triggers silent failures in the simulation engine.
- **Correction on edge cases**: Initially missed the handling of negative income scenarios, which caused division-by-zero errors in the marginal rate logic; fixed by adding a guard clause that defaults to a 0% rate for losses.

--- Story 475: Corruption approval penalty (attempts: 1, 2026-03-18 03:24) ---
- **Non-obvious state coupling**: The approval penalty logic relied on a hidden side effect in the `calculateEffectiveRate` function, where the penalty multiplier was inadvertently shared across concurrent requests until the transaction context was explicitly cleared.
- **Codebase convention**: Financial adjustments in this module always require an immutable `AuditLog` entry before modifying the `AccountState`, even for internal calculations; skipping this step causes silent failures in the downstream reconciliation service.
- **Correction made**: Initially attempted to apply the penalty directly to the cached rate, which caused race conditions; corrected by refactoring to compute the penalty against the raw base rate and applying the delta only during the final commit phase.
